EXECUTIVE SUMMARY 
This document is the report for the DD-WHP Hazard and Operability (HAZOP) study, which 
is part of the development of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields, which are located in Block 46/13, 
Malay - Tho Chu Basin, S. R. Vietnam. The report presents the workshop attendance record, 
the HAZOP records (worksheet) and a summary of the HAZOP recommendations.  
The HAZOP study was conducted in accordance with the Khanh My – Dam Doi Hazard and 
Operability Study Terms of Reference (TOR) (Document No. PTSC-02-TOR-02-Rev A1), 
which was issued prior to the start of the workshop.  
This report should be read in conjunction with the HAZOP ToR document (Document No. 
PTSC-02-TOR-02-Rev A1), International Electrotechnical Commission IEC 61882, Scope of 
Work for the HAZID, HAZOP, and SIL Classification Study (Document No. KDP-OOO-03-
SW-X-0004) as well as the DD-WHP Safety Integrity Level (SIL) Classification Study Report 
(Document No. KDP-DDA-03-RP-X-0021). 
The HAZOP workshop was held at CONTRACTOR’s premises located at Rach Dua ward, Ho 
Chi Minh city, Vietnam on the 05th – 08th of May 2026. The scanned copies of the workshop 
attendance sheets are presented in APPENDIX B of this report. The HAZOP workshop was 
facilitated by a third-party specialist, and the proceedings were recorded by an appointed 
technical scribe (TÜV Rheinland).  
The HAZOP nodes are comprehensively tabulated and defined in APPENDIX C and are 
highlighted on the relevant P&IDs in APPENDIX D. The HAZOP worksheets are presented 
in APPENDIX E of this report.  
Eight recommendations were raised in the EPCI HAZOP workshop. In addition to that, one 
pending recommendation was carried forward from the FEED HAZOP workshop. All 
recommendations are presented in Section 5.3 (Table 3) of this report.

1. 
INTRODUCTION 
PVEP–KHANH MY (herein referred to as COMPANY) is undertaking development of 
Khanh My and Dam Doi fields, which are located in Block 46/13, Malay - Tho Chu 
Basin, S. R. Vietnam, approximately 205 km southwest of Cape Ca Mau and about 30 
km northwest of the Bunga Kekwa field of Block PM3 CAA, with a water depth of 
approximately 53 m. The Project First Gas is expected in Quarter 4 of 2027. 
Location map of Block 46/13 is as shown in Figure 1. 
 
Figure 1 Location map of Block 46/13 
The development of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields will comprise of the following new 
facilities: 
- 
One (1) unmanned wellhead platform KM-WHP. 
- 
One (1) unmanned wellhead platform DD-WHP. 
- 
20” x 6.7 km long FWS rigid pipeline from KM-WHP to DD-WHP. 
- 
20” x 22.0 km long FWS rigid pipeline from DD-WHP to the existing BK-C 
WHRP.

---

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, 
BLOCK 46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM  
 
PROVISION OF EPCI 
DD-WHP HAZARD AND OPERABILITY (HAZOP) STUDY 
REPORT 
 
Document No.: KDP-DDA-03-RP-X-0003-D0 
Page No.: 9 of 88 
 
 
- 
Subsea pig-gable wye fitting which has one inlet spared for Block 46-CN 
Development located at tie-in point approximately 14 km downstream of DD-WHP. 
Development scheme of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields is as shown in Figure 2. 
 
Figure 2 Field development scheme 
In addition, the field development will also consist of modifications to the existing BK- 
C WHRP and BR-A CPP of Block PM3 CAA including: 
- 
A new retrofit 20” riser and clamps, structural deck extension, topside piping and 
valves, pig receiver, allocation gas metering skid, electrical terminations, and 
associated miscellaneous work on BK-C WHRP. 
- 
Upgrade of the existing DCS on BR-A CPP for operation monitoring and remote 
control of KM-WHP and DD-WHP. 
- 
Upgrade of the existing Telecom, Network System on BR-A CPP and HML’s office 
to accommodate the KM-WHP, DD-WHP communication via Digital Microwave 
Radio (DMR) to support operation monitoring and remote control; and data 
transmission from HML’s office to PVEP-KHANH MY’s office. 
Produced fluids of Khanh My and Dam Doi fields will be transferred from KM-WHP 
and DD-WHP to BK-C WHRP, and then to the existing processing facilities at PM3 
Southern Field (PM3S) prior to exporting from Bunga Raya-B platform (BR-B WHRP) 
to Vietnam shore via the existing 18” PM3 - Ca Mau gas export pipeline. Separated 
condensates will be stored in and offloaded later from FSO PM-3 CAA.

---

Page No.: 10 of 88 
 
 
The platforms will be remotely monitored and controlled from BR-A CPP of Block PM3 
CAA as well as being monitored from mainland of Vietnam. Dedicated facilities of PM3S 
will be modified, upgraded or extended to cater for additional production and additional 
facilities to be monitored and controlled. 
KM-WHP and DD-WHP are designed as unmanned platforms for burn down concepts 
and minimum facilities. Each new platform has a total of four (04) conductor slots, and 
each conductor slot is designed to accommodate two (02) individual wells. The facilities 
are designed for simultaneous drilling and production (SIPROD). 
The topsides facilities and subsea pipelines will have a design life of 10 years. The 
platform structures will have a design life of 15 years. 
1.1. PURPOSE 
This report presents the findings of the DD-WHP Hazard and Operability (HAZOP) 
Workshop conducted on 5th to 7th May 2026 as part of the Khanh My – Dam Doi Field 
Development Detailed Engineering phase. 
The HAZOP workshop was conducted to systematically examine the design and 
operation of the DD-WHP facilities by identifying potential process deviations from the 
intended design intent, determining their possible causes and consequences, evaluating 
the adequacy of existing safeguards, and defining recommendations or actions where 
required to reduce risks to an acceptable and ALARP level. 
The workshop was held at the CONTRACTOR’s premises, Complex Building, Rach Dua 
Ward, Ho Chi Minh City, Vietnam, with remote participation facilitated via Microsoft 
Teams.

3. 
HAZOP METHODOLOGY 
The HAZOP methodology was conducted based on the normative reference from 
International Electrotechnical Commission IEC 61882. It provides a guide for HAZOP 
studies of systems utilizing the specific set of guide words defined in this document. It 
also gives guidance on application of the technique and on the HAZOP study procedure, 
including definition, preparation, examination sessions and resulting documentation and 
follow-up. 
3.1 SCOPE OF THE HAZOP STUDY 
The scope of work (document no. KDP-OOO-03-SW-X-0004) covered the “Greenfield” 
as below: 
- 
Greenfield: The development of new unmanned wellhead platform DD-WHP and 
associated pipelines. 
3.2 OVERVIEW 
HAZOP is a step-by-step, qualitative analysis of defined process sections (nodes) to 
identify potential hazards and operability issues. 
The HAZOP study was carried out in a workshop format by a multidisciplinary team, led 
by an external facilitator. Using HAZOP guidewords, the team systematically reviews 
the process drawings to identify significant issues that may arise from deviations from 
the design intent, as well as their consequences. 
The adequacy of existing safeguards were evaluated. If the team considers them 
insufficient, additional safeguards were proposed for implementation in the design. 
The HAZOP process is best understood in the following steps: 
- 
Select the relevant section of the plant (node) 
- 
Define the node’s design intent and normal process conditions 
- 
Select the first (or next) process parameter 
- 
Apply the first (or next) HAZOP guideword to the parameter to generate a deviation 
- 
Identify (through brainstorming) all potential causes of the deviation 
- 
Agree on the credibility (realistic likelihood) of each cause 
- 
Assess the consequences of each credible cause 
- 
Review the existing protection/safeguards against each cause and its consequences 
- 
Evaluate the overall likelihood considering both consequence and protection 
- 
Agree on recommendations for action or further investigation, if needed

---

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, 
BLOCK 46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM  
 
PROVISION OF EPCI 
DD-WHP HAZARD AND OPERABILITY (HAZOP) STUDY 
REPORT 
 
Document No.: KDP-DDA-03-RP-X-0003-D0 
Page No.: 16 of 88 
 
 
- 
Apply the next relevant HAZOP guideword to the same parameter 
- 
Repeat for all parameters of the node 
- 
Move to the next node and repeat the process until the entire system has been 
studied 
A typical HAZOP methodology flowchart is shown in Figure 4.1-1. This HAZOP 
workflow is applicable to all project phases, from design through operation. 
The HAZOP procedure was conducted in accordance with the scope of work for the 
HAZID, HAZOP, and SIL Classification Study (Document No. KDP-OOO-03-SW-X-
0004). The HAZOP process workflow, as outlined in SoW document, is visually 
illustrated in Figure 3: 
 
Figure 3 HAZOP Process Workflow

3.3 HAZOP ASSUMPTIONS 
The HAZOP shall be carried out for the facilities in normal operation. Consequently, it 
shall be assumed that the facilities have been correctly: 
- 
Designed (although design issues will form part of the HAZOP); 
- 
Fabricated 
- 
Installed 
- 
Tested 
- 
Commissioned 
- 
Started-up 
It shall also be assumed that during normal operation, the following are being correctly 
carried out: 
- 
Thickness checks 
- 
Regular vessel inspections 
- 
SIFs tested in accordance with required testing interval and performance standard 
- 
PSVs bench tested in accordance with agreed maintenance management system 
- 
Plant modifications being correctly pressure tested before being put back into 
service 
- 
Maintenance/inspection/testing being carried out by suitably competent engineers 
- 
Operating/Maintenance instructions/procedures/manuals being adhered to

3.5 CAUSE IDENTIFICATION 
The HAZOP study team identified and documented all possible causes within a node, 
guided by the selected parameter and deviation. All identified causes should remain 
specific to the node under study. The team avoided considering double jeopardy scenarios 
and ensure these are not confused with latent failures or interdependencies. 
3.6 ASSESS ALL CREDIBLE CONSEQUENCES 
The HAZOP study team identified and documented the credible consequences of each 
cause, assuming no safeguards are in place. Each consequence statement described the 
initial system response leading to the worst credible consequence. Consequences were 
considered within the relevant node, including upstream or downstream impacts. Where 
applicable, the consequences were further detailed in terms of their potential impact on 
People, Asset, Environment and Reputation. 
3.7 SAFEGUARDS ADEQUACY 
The HAZOP study team identified and documented the existing safeguards, both within 
the node and outside it (upstream or downstream). These safeguards were evaluated in 
relation to their ability to address causes and mitigate consequences. The effectiveness of 
independent safeguards were assessed to ensure that the associated risks were reduced to 
ALARP. 
3.8 SEVERITY RANKING 
The severity categories for consequences to People, Asset, Environment and Reputations 
are presented in APPENDIX Aas per the latest PVEP-KHANH MY HSE Management 
System Manual.

3.9 RISK ASSESSMENT 
During the HAZOP workshop, it was agreed that no risk ranking would be performed. 
Therefore, the PVEP-KHANH MY HSE Risk Assessment Matrix included in 
APPENDIX A is provided for information only.

4. 
HAZOP WORKSHOP 
4.1 SCHEDULE  
The HAZOP workshop was conducted in presence over 3 days between 05th to 7th May 
2026 at the CONTRACTOR’s premises located at Rach Dua ward, Ho Chi Minh city, 
Vietnam and was also conducted online via Microsoft Teams to facilitate remote 
participation. 
4.2 HAZOP PARTICIPANTS  
The HAZOP workshop was facilitated by a third-party specialist, and the proceedings 
were recorded by an appointed technical scribe (TÜV Rheinland). The HAZOP team 
consisted of multi-disciplinary representatives from COMPANY, CONTRACTOR and 
SUB-CONTRACTOR. 
The list of attendees and copy of signed attendance sheet are presented in APPENDIX 
B.

5.3 HAZOP STUDY RECOMMENDATIONS 
A total of eight recommendations were raised during the HAZOP workshop sessions. In 
addition to that, there is one pending recommendation carried forward from the FEED 
HAZOP workshop. 
The complete HAZOP study recommendations are listed in Table 3.  
Table 3 HAZOP Study Recommendation 
No. 
Recommendations 
Responsibility 
EPCI 
1 
Review the requirement for PSV-1931A/B sized for check valve 
leakage. The overpressure protection from the HIPPS will isolate 
the system in 2s as per specification and this may be considered 
sufficient. Reference to P&ID KDP-DDA-03-DW-B-19002.01.  
PMC 
CONTRACTOR 
2 
Review the configuration of the HIPPS bleed-off line via XV-
1120 to the vent and compare the option of using the PSV 
downstream of HIPPS. 
PMC 
CONTRACTOR 
3 
Review the positive isolation requirement upstream of MOV-
1921 (export launcher N-1920).  
PMC 
CONTRACTOR

the CD transfer pump (P-5020A/B). 
PMC 
CONTRACTOR

the ignited vent in case of thermal sensor (TS-5640) unavailable 
or due for maintenance. 
PMC 
CONTRACTOR

of PCV fail closed and provide safeguard to detect or maintain N2 
blanket pressure at all times.

APPENDIX A – RISK RANKING [FOR REFERENCE ONLY]  
Note 1: 
During the HAZOP workshop, it was agreed that no risk ranking would be performed. Therefore, the PVEP-
KHANH MY HSE Risk Assessment Matrix is provided for information only. 
Note 2: 
The PVEP-KHANH MY HSE Risk Assessment Matrix, as defined in the PVEP-KHANH MY HSE Management 
System Manual, shall be used for qualitative assessment of HSE risks across all PVEP-KHANH MY operations, 
including Contractors. 
Note 3: 
Hazards and their associated risks are to be evaluated using this matrix, and all risks shall be managed to a level 
that is As Low As Reasonably Practicable (ALARP).  
The applicable Severity Levels, Likelihood Categories and Risk Assessment Matrix are below. 
 
 
Figure 4 HSE Risk Assessment Matrix

KHANH MY – DAM DOI FIELDS DEVELOPMENT PROJECT, 
BLOCK 46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM  
 
PROVISION OF EPCI 
DD-WHP HAZARD AND OPERABILITY (HAZOP) STUDY 
REPORT 
 
Document No.: KDP-DDA-03-RP-X-0003-D0 
Page No.: 26 of 88 
 
 
Table 4 Severity Categories – Impact on People 
IMPACT ON PEOPLE 
Severity 
Description 
1 
Insignificant 
First aid injury or slight health effects not affecting work performance or 
causing disability e.g. first aid injury, exposure to non-hazardous dusts. 
2 
Minor 
Medical Treatment Case, Restricted Work Case, Lost Time Injury or minor 
health effects (involving health hazards capable of minor health effects 
which are reversible, e.g. irritant agents, defatting agents, food poisoning 
bacteria) affecting work performance, such as restriction to work activities 
or a need to take a few days to fully recover. 
3 
Moderate 
Permanent Partial Disability, significant health effects (capable of 
irreversible health damage without loss of life, e.g. noise, poor manual 
handling tasks, hand/arm vibration, chemicals causing systemic effects, 
sensitizers) , exposure to possible human or animal carcinogens, or results 
of injury/illness in the lower categories (category 1 & 2 above) which affect 
performance in the longer term such as prolonged absence from work for 
more than 4 days. 
4 
Major 
Permanent Total Disability, single fatality from accident or occupational 
illness or major health effects caused by health hazards capable of 
irreversible damage with serious disability or death e.g. exposure to 
corrosives, probable human carcinogens, extreme heat and cold, 
psychosocial risk factors. 
5 
Catastrophic 
Multiple fatalities or Multiple Permanent Total Disability from accident or 
occupational illness caused by health hazards with the potential to cause 
multiple fatalities, e.g. chemicals with acute toxic effects (hydrogen 
sulphide, carbon monoxide), known human carcinogens

Table 6 Severity Categories – Impact on Environment 
IMPACT ON ENVIRONMENT 
Severity 
Description (Meet one OR all of the criteria) 
1 
Insignificant 
1. Spill/leak causing negligible impact to local environment, contained 
within the secondary containment and does not reach water and soil, and 
no volatilization to atmosphere. 
2. Noise, air emission, discharges not exceeding company or legislative 
limits. 
2 
Minor 
1. Spill/leak contained within secondary containment: 
• causing volatilization 
to atmosphere 
• causing limited contamination of soil or water within the containment 
area 
• causing non-permanent impacts to the environment 
2. Noise, air emission, discharges not exceeding legislative limit but 
exceeding company limits (where available). 
3. No immediate cumulative and/or delayed effect. 
3 
Moderate 
1. Spill/leak causing limited contamination to soil or water outside the 
secondary containment but remain contained within facility perimeter 
(for onshore operation) ** OR resulting in Potential Consequence A, B 
or C below. 
2. Noise, air emission, discharges not exceeding company or legislative 
limits OR resulting in Potential Consequence A, B or C below. 
Note: 
Potential Consequence 
A. Cumulative and/or delayed environmental impact 
B. Short term recovery action <1 month 
C. Rehabilitation period <6 months 
**For offshore operation, spill/leak into marine environment but limited 
potential contamination to marine water. 
4 
Major 
1. Spill/leak spreading outside the facility perimeter, managed to be 
contained/recovered but causing major contamination OR resulting in 
Potential Consequence A, B or C below. 
2. Noise, air emission, discharges exceeding legislative limit with possible 
prosecution OR resulting in Potential Consequence A below. 
Note: 
Potential Consequence 
A. Immediate effect with serious damage to environment 
B. Medium term recovery action (1-3 months)

---

BLOCK 46/13, OFFSHORE VIETNAM  
 
PROVISION OF EPCI

Page No.: 29 of 88 
 
 
IMPACT ON ENVIRONMENT 
Severity 
Description (Meet one OR all of the criteria) 
C. Rehabilitation period 6-12 months 
5 
Massive impact 
1. Spill/leak spreading outside the facility perimeter, causing massive 
contamination OR resulting in Potential Consequence A, B or C below. 
2. Noise, air emission, discharges resulting in legal prosecution with 
possible shutdown of facility OR resulting in Potential Consequence A 
below. 
Note: 
Potential Consequence 
A. Severe environmental damage 
B. Long term recovery action (>3 months) 
C. Rehabilitation period >12 months

Table 7 Severity Categories – Impact on Reputation 
IMPACT ON REPUTATION 
Severity 
Description (Meet one OR all of the criteria) 
1 
Insignificant 
Slight Impact 
 Public awareness may exist, but there is no public concern. 
2 
Minor 
Limited Impact 
 Local public concern or complaints. 
 Local media and/or local political attention with potentially 
negative impact on company operations. 
3 
Moderate 
Considerable Impact 
 Regional public concern. Extensive adverse attention in local 
media. 
 National media and/or regional political attention resulting in 
negative impact on company operations. 
 Adverse stance of local government and/or action Groups. 
4 
Major 
National Impact 
 National public concern. Extensive adverse attention in the 
national media. 
 Regional/national policies with potentially restrictive measures 
and/or impact on grant of licenses** 
 Mobilization of pressure or action groups. 
5 
Catastrophic 
International Impact 
 International public attention. Extensive adverse attention in 
international media. 
 National/international policies with potentially severe impact on 
access to new areas, grants of licenses** and/or tax legislation.

NOTE 15
NOTES :
1.
CHOKE VALVE CAN BE OPENED/CLOSED LOCALLY OR REMOTELY FROM PCS.
2.
PROVISION FOR FLUSHING/GEL BREAKING CONNECTOR.
3.
SELF EQUALIZATION VALVE.
4.
BEAN SIZE INDICATION OF VALVE OPENING TO BE PROVIDED IN PCS FOR EASY
REFERENCE TO PRODUCTION PLANNING.
5.
PIPE TAPPING IS AT 5 OR 7 O'CLOCK FOR LIQUID SAMPLING AT HORIZONTAL PIPE.
6.
PIPE TAPPING IS AT 12 O'CLOCK FOR GAS SAMPLING AT HORIZONTAL PIPE.
7.
CORROSION COUPON TO BE LOCATED ON THE HORIZONTAL SECTION OF THE
FLOWLINE AT 12 O'CLOCK.
8.
SOLID TARGET TEE SHALL BE USED IN BENDS SECTION OF FLOWLINE TO MINIMIZE
FLOW EROSION OF THE BEND SECTION DUE TO HIGH VELOCITY DISCHARGE FROM
CHOKE VALVE.
9.
FLANGE SPOOL PIECE TO BE USED FOR OFFSHORE HOOK-UP DURING WELL TIE IN
(SIPROD MODE) AND MAINTENANCE.
10. FOR FUTURE TIE-IN.
11. DIAPHRAGM SEAL IS REQUIRED FOR PT/PG  DUE TO WAXY CONDY.
12. SPARE CONNECTION FOR SAND PROBE.
13. MINIMUM OF 0.6m(W) X 2.5M(L)   CLEARANCE IS REQUIRED FOR ONLINE RETRIEVAL.

NOTES :
1.
MINIMUM LENGTH SHALL BE EQUAL TO MAXIMUM LENGTH OF REGULAR PIG ONLY
(INTELLIGENT PIG).
2.
VALVE INTERNAL DIAMETER SHALL BE THE SAME AS PIPELINE INTERNAL DIAMETER.
3.
LINE PIPE AND BEND ARE FREE-ISSUED BY COMPANY.
4.
LAUNCHER SHALL BE DESIGNED FOR REGULAR PIGGING.
5.
SAFETY LOCK DEVICE SHALL BE PROVIDED TO ENSURE THAT THE LAUNCHER
CLOSURE DOOR CANNOT BE OPENED IF THE BARREL IS STILL PRESSURIZED.
6.
HIGH (PG-1921) AND LOW (PG-1922) RANGE PRESSURE GAUGES TO BE INSTALLED ON
THE LAUNCHER. THE LOW RANGE PRESSURE GAUGE TO BE SUITABLE FOR 0-1 BARG
PRESSURE READING AND IT SHALL BE PROVIDED WITH GAUGE SAVER. PRESSURE
GAUGES SHALL BE READABLE FROM LAUNCHER END CLOSURE.
7.
PRESSURE GAUGE TO BE VISIBLE TO OPERATOR FOR MANUAL DEPRESSURIZATION OF
LAUNCHER AND OPENING OF BARREL DOOR.
8.
NITROGEN PURGING IS REQUIRED DURING DRAINING ACTIVITY DUE TO LAUNCHER
AND CLOSED DRAIN HEADER LOCATE AT THE SAME PLATFORM DECK.
9.
CONNECTION FOR NITROGEN PURGING AND WATER FLUSHING.

133 barg against well CITHP against well CITHP is 187 
barg. Therefore, the exceedance factor is 1.4x the design 
pressure which could result in flange/gasket leaks, if 
ignited fire/explosion.

Consequences 
Current Safeguards 
Recommendations 
Responsibility 
Remarks 
High Temperature 
Ambient temperature.  
High vapour pressure in the Diesel storage tank (T-5720) 
and in the Diesel tote tank (T-5721), and higher venting 
rate.  
Vent to safe location away from high temperature sources 
such as exhaust. 
 
 
 
Low Temperature 
No causes identified.  
 
 
 
 
 
High Level 
Failure during top-up operation. 
Overfill in the Diesel storage tank (T-5720) and potential 
for high level in the Open drain tank resulting in 
contamination of the water compartment and spill to the 
sea. 
LIAH-5723 will alarm high level in the Diesel storage tank with 
an audible alarm horn located near to the bunkering filling 
station.  
 
 
 
Low Level 
Failure to stop the pump when the 
level is reached during DEG day 
tank top up. 
Initiating Event13.1.1.1 
Low level in the Diesel storage tank (T-5720) and potential 
for pump damage if it runs dry. Potential for overflow in the 
DEG day tank and spilled to the wellhead service deck via 
the vent. 
 
Asset: Direct damage cost from USD2,500 to USD25,000. 
LOPA Scenario: 13.1 
LIAL-5723 will alarm low level in the Diesel storage tank. 
 
 
 
LZALL-5721 will trip the Diesel pump and initiate an audible 
alarm horn.  
Insufficient inventory of Diesel 
onboard of the wellhead platform 
and DEG is running low.  
Initiating Event13.2.1.1 
In case of insufficient Diesel onboard, the level in DEG day 
tank and Diesel tote tank, will also be low. DEG day tank 
will also be emptied resulting in loss of power to the main 
users. 
 
Note: The DEG will be in operation during the operator 
visit on the wellhead platform. 
 
Asset: Direct Damage cost less than USD2,500. 
LOPA Scenario: 13.2 
Diesel consumption and Diesel top-up procedure. 
 
 
 
LIAL-5723 will alarm low level in the Diesel storage tank. 
LZAL-7120 (pre-alarm) /LZALL-7120 trip the DEG and initiate 
an audible alarm horn.
